# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce artifacts** — Express all code changes as **unified diffs** in your output artifact (e.g., `fix_patch` fields in review.json, or a standalone `solution.patch` file). Do NOT edit source files directly — there are none in your workspace.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# big-code-django-arch-001: Django ORM Query Compilation Pipeline

## Task

Map the Django ORM query compilation pipeline from QuerySet to SQL. Trace how a high-level QuerySet API call (e.g., `Model.objects.filter(...)`) is lazily constructed, compiled into SQL, and executed against the database, including the expression/lookup system and backend-specific vendor dispatch.

## Context

- **Repository**: django/django (Python, ~350K LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: django/db/models/ and django/db/backends/ — the ORM query compilation layer

## Requirements

1. Identify all files involved in the query compilation pipeline (Manager, QuerySet, Query, Compiler, Expressions, Lookups, Backend)
2. Trace the dependency chain from `Manager.get_queryset()` through lazy query building, compilation via `as_sql()`, to `execute_sql()`
3. Document the `compile(node)` vendor dispatch mechanism (`as_{vendor}()` pattern)
4. Explain how the WhereNode tree structure, Expression protocol, and Lookup system compose to produce SQL

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

71-assistanttext-
I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Django ORM query compilation pipeline and written it to `/logs/agent/solution.md`. Here's what I discovered:

## Key Findings

**Entry Point Chain:**
- `Manager.get_queryset()` → Creates QuerySet with a Query object
- QuerySet lazy-builds the Query (no SQL yet)
- On evaluation, `QuerySet.__iter__()` calls `compiler = query.get_compiler()` and `execute_sql()`

**Query Representation:**
The Query class is the AST that stores:
- `alias_map` — JOIN table aliases
- `where` — WhereNode tree of filter predicates
- `annotations`, `select`, `group_by`, `order_by`

**Compilation Pipeline:**
1. **Query.get_compiler()** — Retrieves backend-specific compiler via `connection.ops.compiler()`
2. **SQLCompiler.as_sql()** — Assembles SELECT/FROM/WHERE/GROUP BY/HAVING/ORDER BY by recursively compiling expressions
3. **compile() vendor dispatch** — Tries `as_{vendor}()` method before `as_sql()`
4. **WhereNode.as_sql()** — Recursively compiles Lookup children, joins with AND/OR/XOR
5. **Lookup.as_sql()** — Compiles left/right operands and formats as SQL condition

**Key Design Patterns:**
- **Lazy Evaluation** — Query built without executing until needed
- **Visitor/Compiler Pattern** — Each Expression/Lookup knows how to generate its own SQL
- **Vendor Dispatch** — Clean separation of database-specific SQL via `as_{vendor}()` convention
- **Tree-Structured WHERE** — WhereNode supports nested logical filters
- **Two-Phase Resolution** — Query AST built first, then traversed for SQL generation

The analysis document includes all files examined, the complete dependency chain, detailed component responsibilities, data flow description, and interface contracts between components.

  "content": "# Django ORM Query Compilation Pipeline Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core QuerySet & Manager (Entry Points)\n- **django/db/models/manager.py** \u2014 Manager class providing `get_queryset()` entry point that creates QuerySet instances; serves as the public API surface for model queries\n- **django/db/models/query.py** \u2014 QuerySet class implementing lazy query construction; holds reference to Query object and manages result caching, filtering, ordering, and iteration; delegates SQL generation to Query compiler\n\n### SQL Query Representation Layer\n- **django/db/models/sql/query.py** \u2014 Query class representing abstract SQL statement structure; stores table aliases, WHERE conditions, JOIN information, annotations, GROUP BY, ORDER BY; implements `get_compiler()` method for obtaining backend-specific compiler\n- **django/db/models/sql/where.py** \u2014 WhereNode class representing tree-structured WHERE clause predicates using AND/OR/XOR connectors; recursively compiles child expressions to SQL\n\n### SQL Compilation Layer\n- **django/db/models/sql/compiler.py** \u2014 SQLCompiler class (and subclasses SQLInsertCompiler, SQLUpdateCompiler, SQLDeleteCompiler) that generates SQL from Query; implements `as_sql()` method assembling SELECT, FROM, WHERE, GROUP BY, HAVING, ORDER BY, LIMIT/OFFSET clauses; implements `execute_sql()` for executing compiled SQL against database\n- **django/db/models/sql/datastructures.py** \u2014 BaseTable, Join, MultiJoin classes representing table aliases and JOIN structures in query\n\n### Expression System (Composable SQL Building Blocks)\n- **django/db/models/expressions.py** \u2014 BaseExpression class defining Expression protocol with `as_sql()` method for SQL code generation; subclasses include Value (literals), F (field references), Col (column references), Case/When (conditional expressions), Func (functions), CombinedExpression (arithmetic/bitwise operations)\n- Each expression implements:\n  - `as_sql(compiler, connection)` \u2192 returns `(sql_string, params_tuple)`\n  - `resolve_expression(query, ...)` for lazy resolution of field references and type inference\n  - `get_source_expressions()` / `set_source_expressions()` for AST traversal\n\n### Lookup System (WHERE Clause Predicates)\n- **django/db/models/lookups.py** \u2014 Lookup class (extends Expression) representing filter predicates (e.g., `field=value`, `field__gt=value`); transforms filter arguments into SQL conditions\n  - BuiltinLookup subclass with `as_sql()` assembling LEFT operator RIGHT (e.g., `\"age > %s\"`)\n  - Lookup.process_lhs() / process_rhs() compile left and right operands separately\n  - Transform class for chained lookups (e.g., `date__year__gt`)\n\n### Backend Operations & Vendor-Specific Compilation\n- **django/db/backends/base/operations.py** \u2014 BaseDatabaseOperations class with `compiler(compiler_name)` method returning backend-specific compiler class; manages quote names, type casts, database-specific SQL syntax\n- **django/db/backends/{postgresql,mysql,sqlite3,oracle}/compiler.py** \u2014 Backend-specific SQLCompiler subclasses overriding `as_sql()` for dialect-specific SQL generation (e.g., PostgreSQL RETURNING, MySQL UPDATE...ORDER BY)\n- **django/db/backends/{postgresql,mysql,sqlite3,oracle}/operations.py** \u2014 Backend-specific operations classes setting `compiler_module` attribute pointing to backend's compiler module\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. **Entry Point: Manager.get_queryset()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/manager.py:150\n   - Returns a QuerySet instance initialized with the model and a fresh Query object\n\n### 2. **QuerySet Lazy Construction**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/query.py:303\u2013336\n   - QuerySet stores a Query object (`self._query = sql.Query(self.model)`)\n   - When methods like `.filter()`, `.exclude()`, `.values()`, `.annotate()` are called, they modify the internal Query object (via methods like `add_filter()`, `add_annotation()`, etc.) but don't execute the query\n   - Result is cached only when the QuerySet is evaluated (via `__iter__`, `list()`, or database fetch)\n\n### 3. **Query Representation Build-up**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/query.py:231\u2013410\n   - Query class stores:\n     - `alias_map`: JOIN table aliases and their types\n     - `where`: WhereNode tree of filter predicates\n     - `annotations`: {name \u2192 Expression} for aggregations\n     - `select`: tuple of (Expression, alias) pairs for SELECT columns\n     - `group_by`, `order_by`, `distinct`: query modifiers\n   - Query.filter() calls `add_filter()` which:\n     - Parses lookup strings (e.g., `\"author__name__icontains\"`) into field traversals\n     - Calls `setup_joins()` to add necessary JOINs to alias_map\n     - Creates Lookup instances and adds them to WhereNode\n\n### 4. **Compiler Instantiation: Query.get_compiler()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/query.py:369\u2013376\n   ```python\n   def get_compiler(self, using=None, connection=None, elide_empty=True):\n       connection = connections[using]\n       return connection.ops.compiler(self.compiler)(\n           self, connection, using, elide_empty\n       )\n   ```\n   - Looks up `connection.ops.compiler()` which dynamically loads backend-specific compiler\n   - Example: PostgreSQL has `compiler_module = \"django.db.backends.postgresql.compiler\"`\n   - Instantiates appropriate SQLCompiler subclass (SQLCompiler, SQLInsertCompiler, etc.)\n\n### 5. **Compiler Setup: pre_sql_setup()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:80\u201394\n   - Called automatically during `as_sql()` compilation\n   - Resolves JOINs, sets up SELECT columns via `get_select()`\n   - Splits WhereNode into WHERE / HAVING / QUALIFY clauses via `split_having_qualify()`\n   - Computes GROUP BY expressions via `get_group_by()`\n\n### 6. **SQL Generation: SQLCompiler.as_sql()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:763\u2013988\n   - Main method that assembles final SQL from Query representation\n   - Iterates through SELECT expressions and compiles each via `compile(expression)`\n   - For WHERE clause: calls `compiler.compile(where_node)` \u2192 WhereNode.as_sql()\n   - For each child in WhereNode: recursively calls `compiler.compile(child)` on Lookup instances\n   - Assembles result list: `[\"SELECT\", columns, \"FROM\", tables, \"WHERE\", conditions, ...]`\n   - Returns tuple: `(sql_string, params_list)`\n\n### 7. **Expression/Lookup Compilation: compile() Vendor Dispatch**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:580\u2013586\n   ```python\n   def compile(self, node):\n       vendor_impl = getattr(node, \"as_\" + self.connection.vendor, None)\n       if vendor_impl:\n           sql, params = vendor_impl(self, self.connection)\n       else:\n           sql, params = node.as_sql(self, self.connection)\n       return sql, params\n   ```\n   - **Vendor Dispatch Pattern**: For each node (Expression, Lookup, etc.), tries backend-specific method first\n   - Example: PostgreSQL backend tries `as_postgresql()` before falling back to `as_sql()`\n   - Each backend in django/db/backends/{vendor}/ can override compilation for vendor-specific SQL\n\n### 8. **WHERE Clause Tree Compilation: WhereNode.as_sql()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/where.py:116\u2013188\n   - Recursively compiles each child by calling `compiler.compile(child)` (usually a Lookup)\n   - Joins compiled SQL with connector string: `\" AND \".join(results)` or `\" OR \".join(results)`\n   - Handles XOR by converting to OR + MOD expression on databases without XOR support\n   - Returns parenthesized result for precedence\n\n### 9. **Lookup Compilation: BuiltinLookup.as_sql()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/lookups.py:237\u2013242\n   ```python\n   def as_sql(self, compiler, connection):\n       lhs_sql, params = self.process_lhs(compiler, connection)\n       rhs_sql, rhs_params = self.process_rhs(compiler, connection)\n       rhs_sql = self.get_rhs_op(connection, rhs_sql)\n       return \"%s %s\" % (lhs_sql, rhs_sql), (*params, *rhs_params)\n   ```\n   - Compiles left operand (e.g., field column reference) via process_lhs()\n   - Compiles right operand (e.g., filter value) via process_rhs()\n   - Looks up operator from `connection.operators[lookup_name]` (e.g., operators['exact'] = '%s = %s')\n   - Returns formatted SQL and combined parameters\n\n### 10. **SQL Execution: SQLCompiler.execute_sql()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:1601\u20131673\n   - Calls `as_sql()` to get SQL string and parameters\n   - Gets database cursor via `connection.cursor()` or `connection.chunked_cursor()`\n   - Executes: `cursor.execute(sql, params)`\n   - Returns results based on result_type (MULTI, SINGLE, ROW_COUNT, CURSOR)\n\n### 11. **Results Processing & Model Instantiation**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/query.py:88\u2013163 (ModelIterable.__iter__)\n   - Compiler.execute_sql() returns raw database rows\n   - For each row: calls `model_cls.from_db()` to instantiate model object\n   - Populates related objects, deferred fields, and annotations\n   - Yields model instance\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n1. **Lazy Evaluation**\n   - QuerySet builds Query representation without executing\n   - SQL only generated when QuerySet is iterated or explicitly evaluated\n   - Enables chaining: `Model.objects.filter().exclude().values()`\n\n2. **Visitor/Compiler Pattern**\n   - SQLCompiler \"visits\" Expression/Lookup nodes, calling their `as_sql()` method\n   - Each node type responsible for its own SQL representation\n   - Enables extensibility: custom expressions/lookups just implement `as_sql()`\n\n3. **Vendor Dispatch via as_{vendor}() Convention**\n   - Expression/Lookup classes can define `as_postgresql()`, `as_mysql()`, `as_oracle()`, `as_sqlite()` methods\n   - SQLCompiler.compile() checks for vendor method before calling generic `as_sql()`\n   - Allows clean database-specific SQL overrides without polymorphic class hierarchies\n\n4. **Tree-Structured WHERE Clauses**\n   - WhereNode extends tree.Node with AND/OR/XOR connectors\n   - Supports nested logical expressions: `(field1=A AND field2=B) OR (field3=C)`\n   - Separates WHERE from HAVING via split_having_qualify() for aggregation correctness\n\n5. **Two-Phase Resolution**\n   - Phase 1: QuerySet.filter() builds Query AST (JOINs, WHERE nodes, annotations)\n   - Phase 2: SQLCompiler.as_sql() traverses AST and generates SQL (calls resolve_expression on expressions)\n   - Enables deferred field reference resolution and optimization\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Responsibility |\n|-----------|---|\n| **QuerySet** | High-level filtering API, result caching, iteration protocol |\n| **Query** | Represent query structure (tables, JOINs, WHERE, GROUP BY); store metadata |\n| **SQLCompiler** | Traverse Query AST and assemble SELECT/FROM/WHERE/GROUP BY/ORDER BY SQL clauses |\n| **WhereNode** | Tree representation of filter predicates; compile to WHERE/HAVING clauses |\n| **Expression** | Represent query values/operations; generate SQL fragments for themselves |\n| **Lookup** | Represent filter predicates (e.g., field=value); compile to SQL conditions |\n| **Backend Compiler** | Database-specific SQL dialect generation; override as_sql() for vendor features |\n\n### Data Flow Description\n\n1. **Filter Definition Phase**\n   ```\n   Model.objects.filter(name='John', age__gt=18)\n   \u2193\n   QuerySet._filter_or_exclude_inplace() parses kwargs\n   \u2193\n   Query.add_filter() creates Lookup('name', 'John'), Lookup('age__gt', 18)\n   \u2193\n   WhereNode.children = [Lookup(...), Lookup(...)]\n   \u2193\n   Query.setup_joins() adds necessary JOINs to alias_map\n   ```\n\n2. **Compilation Phase**\n   ```\n   SQLCompiler.as_sql()\n   \u2193\n   for each expression in self.select:\n       compile(expression) \u2192 expression.as_sql(compiler, connection)\n   \u2193\n   compile(where_node)\n       \u2193 WhereNode.as_sql()\n       \u251c\u2500 for each child (Lookup):\n       \u2502   \u251c\u2500 compile(child)\n       \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Lookup.as_sql()\n       \u2502   \u2502       \u251c\u2500 process_lhs() \u2192 compile(lhs_expression)\n       \u2502   \u2502       \u2514\u2500 process_rhs() \u2192 compile(rhs_value)\n       \u2502   \u2514\u2500 accumulate SQL and params\n       \u2514\u2500 \" AND \".join() or \" OR \".join()\n   \u2193\n   Result: (\"SELECT id, name FROM app_model WHERE name = %s AND age > %s\", ['John', 18])\n   ```\n\n3. **Execution Phase**\n   ```\n   cursor.execute(sql, params)\n   \u2193\n   Database returns raw rows\n   \u2193\n   for each row:\n       Model.from_db(db, fields, row_data) \u2192 Model instance\n   \u2193\n   QuerySet iteration yields Model instances\n   ```\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n1. **Expression Protocol**\n   - `as_sql(compiler, connection)` \u2192 `(sql_string, params_list)`\n   - `resolve_expression(query, ...)` \u2192 resolved Expression instance\n   - `get_source_expressions()` \u2192 `[expr, ...]`\n\n2. **Compiler Protocol**\n   - `compile(node)` \u2192 `(sql_string, params_list)` (dispatcher to as_sql/as_vendor)\n   - `setup_query()` \u2192 side effect: sets self.select, self.klass_info, self.annotation_col_map\n   - `execute_sql(result_type)` \u2192 results (rows, row count, cursor, or empty)\n\n3. **Lookup Protocol** (extends Expression)\n   - `process_lhs(compiler, connection)` \u2192 `(sql_string, params_list)`\n   - `process_rhs(compiler, connection)` \u2192 `(sql_string, params_list)`\n   - `get_rhs_op(connection, rhs_sql)` \u2192 formatted operator + RHS (e.g., `\"= %s\"`)\n\n4. **Backend Operations Protocol**\n   - `compiler(compiler_name)` \u2192 SQLCompiler class\n   - `quote_name(identifier)` \u2192 quoted identifier\n   - Database feature flags (supports_select_for_update, has_bulk_insert, etc.)\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nDjango's ORM query compilation follows a **lazy evaluation + multi-phase compilation** architecture. High-level QuerySet operations build an abstract SQL representation (Query object with annotations, JOINs, and WhereNode predicates) without executing. When evaluation is triggered, the **SQLCompiler walks the Query AST and recursively compiles each Expression/Lookup via the as_sql() protocol**, using a **vendor dispatch pattern** (as_{vendor}() methods) to support database-specific dialects. The **WhereNode tree** elegantly handles nested logical filters, while the **Lookup system** abstracts filter syntax (\"field__lookup=value\") into bidirectional SQL compilation. This design separates query building from SQL generation, enabling complex query composition while remaining flexible for database vendor customization.\n",

**File**: django/db/models/manager.py:150\n   - Returns a QuerySet instance initialized with the model and a fresh Query object\n\n### 2. **QuerySet Lazy Construction**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/query.py:303\u2013336\n   - QuerySet stores a Query object (`self._query = sql.Query(self.model)`)\n   - When methods like `.filter()`, `.exclude()`, `.values()`, `.annotate()` are called, they modify the internal Query object (via methods like `add_filter()`, `add_annotation()`, etc.) but don't execute the query\n   - Result is cached only when the QuerySet is evaluated (via `__iter__`, `list()`, or database fetch)\n\n### 3. **Query Representation Build-up**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/query.py:231\u2013410\n   - Query class stores:\n     - `alias_map`: JOIN table aliases and their types\n     - `where`: WhereNode tree of filter predicates\n     - `annotations`: {name \u2192 Expression} for aggregations\n     - `select`: tuple of (Expression, alias) pairs for SELECT columns\n     - `group_by`, `order_by`, `distinct`: query modifiers\n   - Query.filter() calls `add_filter()` which:\n     - Parses lookup strings (e.g., `\"author__name__icontains\"`) into field traversals\n     - Calls `setup_joins()` to add necessary JOINs to alias_map\n     - Creates Lookup instances and adds them to WhereNode\n\n### 4. **Compiler Instantiation: Query.get_compiler()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/query.py:369\u2013376\n   ```python\n   def get_compiler(self, using=None, connection=None, elide_empty=True):\n       connection = connections[using]\n       return connection.ops.compiler(self.compiler)(\n           self, connection, using, elide_empty\n       )\n   ```\n   - Looks up `connection.ops.compiler()` which dynamically loads backend-specific compiler\n   - Example: PostgreSQL has `compiler_module = \"django.db.backends.postgresql.compiler\"`\n   - Instantiates appropriate SQLCompiler subclass (SQLCompiler, SQLInsertCompiler, etc.)\n\n### 5. **Compiler Setup: pre_sql_setup()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:80\u201394\n   - Called automatically during `as_sql()` compilation\n   - Resolves JOINs, sets up SELECT columns via `get_select()`\n   - Splits WhereNode into WHERE / HAVING / QUALIFY clauses via `split_having_qualify()`\n   - Computes GROUP BY expressions via `get_group_by()`\n\n### 6. **SQL Generation: SQLCompiler.as_sql()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:763\u2013988\n   - Main method that assembles final SQL from Query representation\n   - Iterates through SELECT expressions and compiles each via `compile(expression)`\n   - For WHERE clause: calls `compiler.compile(where_node)` \u2192 WhereNode.as_sql()\n   - For each child in WhereNode: recursively calls `compiler.compile(child)` on Lookup instances\n   - Assembles result list: `[\"SELECT\", columns, \"FROM\", tables, \"WHERE\", conditions, ...]`\n   - Returns tuple: `(sql_string, params_list)`\n\n### 7. **Expression/Lookup Compilation: compile() Vendor Dispatch**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:580\u2013586\n   ```python\n   def compile(self, node):\n       vendor_impl = getattr(node, \"as_\" + self.connection.vendor, None)\n       if vendor_impl:\n           sql, params = vendor_impl(self, self.connection)\n       else:\n           sql, params = node.as_sql(self, self.connection)\n       return sql, params\n   ```\n   - **Vendor Dispatch Pattern**: For each node (Expression, Lookup, etc.), tries backend-specific method first\n   - Example: PostgreSQL backend tries `as_postgresql()` before falling back to `as_sql()`\n   - Each backend in django/db/backends/{vendor}/ can override compilation for vendor-specific SQL\n\n### 8. **WHERE Clause Tree Compilation: WhereNode.as_sql()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/where.py:116\u2013188\n   - Recursively compiles each child by calling `compiler.compile(child)` (usually a Lookup)\n   - Joins compiled SQL with connector string: `\" AND \".join(results)` or `\" OR \".join(results)`\n   - Handles XOR by converting to OR + MOD expression on databases without XOR support\n   - Returns parenthesized result for precedence\n\n### 9. **Lookup Compilation: BuiltinLookup.as_sql()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/lookups.py:237\u2013242\n   ```python\n   def as_sql(self, compiler, connection):\n       lhs_sql, params = self.process_lhs(compiler, connection)\n       rhs_sql, rhs_params = self.process_rhs(compiler, connection)\n       rhs_sql = self.get_rhs_op(connection, rhs_sql)\n       return \"%s %s\" % (lhs_sql, rhs_sql), (*params, *rhs_params)\n   ```\n   - Compiles left operand (e.g., field column reference) via process_lhs()\n   - Compiles right operand (e.g., filter value) via process_rhs()\n   - Looks up operator from `connection.operators[lookup_name]` (e.g., operators['exact'] = '%s = %s')\n   - Returns formatted SQL and combined parameters\n\n### 10. **SQL Execution: SQLCompiler.execute_sql()**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/sql/compiler.py:1601\u20131673\n   - Calls `as_sql()` to get SQL string and parameters\n   - Gets database cursor via `connection.cursor()` or `connection.chunked_cursor()`\n   - Executes: `cursor.execute(sql, params)`\n   - Returns results based on result_type (MULTI, SINGLE, ROW_COUNT, CURSOR)\n\n### 11. **Results Processing & Model Instantiation**\n   - **File**: django/db/models/query.py:88\u2013163 (ModelIterable.__iter__)\n   - Compiler.execute_sql() returns raw database rows\n   - For each row: calls `model_cls.from_db()` to instantiate model object\n   - Populates related objects, deferred fields, and annotations\n   - Yields model instance\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n1. **Lazy Evaluation**\n   - QuerySet builds Query representation without executing\n   - SQL only generated when QuerySet is iterated or explicitly evaluated\n   - Enables chaining: `Model.objects.filter().exclude().values()`\n\n2. **Visitor/Compiler Pattern**\n   - SQLCompiler \"visits\" Expression/Lookup nodes, calling their `as_sql()` method\n   - Each node type responsible for its own SQL representation\n   - Enables extensibility: custom expressions/lookups just implement `as_sql()`\n\n3. **Vendor Dispatch via as_{vendor}() Convention**\n   - Expression/Lookup classes can define `as_postgresql()`, `as_mysql()`, `as_oracle()`, `as_sqlite()` methods\n   - SQLCompiler.compile() checks for vendor method before calling generic `as_sql()`\n   - Allows clean database-specific SQL overrides without polymorphic class hierarchies\n\n4. **Tree-Structured WHERE Clauses**\n   - WhereNode extends tree.Node with AND/OR/XOR connectors\n   - Supports nested logical expressions: `(field1=A AND field2=B) OR (field3=C)`\n   - Separates WHERE from HAVING via split_having_qualify() for aggregation correctness\n\n5. **Two-Phase Resolution**\n   - Phase 1: QuerySet.filter() builds Query AST (JOINs, WHERE nodes, annotations)\n   - Phase 2: SQLCompiler.as_sql() traverses AST and generates SQL (calls resolve_expression on expressions)\n   - Enables deferred field reference resolution and optimization\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Responsibility |\n|-----------|---|\n| **QuerySet** | High-level filtering API, result caching, iteration protocol |\n| **Query** | Represent query structure (tables, JOINs, WHERE, GROUP BY); store metadata |\n| **SQLCompiler** | Traverse Query AST and assemble SELECT/FROM/WHERE/GROUP BY/ORDER BY SQL clauses |\n| **WhereNode** | Tree representation of filter predicates; compile to WHERE/HAVING clauses |\n| **Expression** | Represent query values/operations; generate SQL fragments for themselves |\n| **Lookup** | Represent filter predicates (e.g., field=value); compile to SQL conditions |\n| **Backend Compiler** | Database-specific SQL dialect generation; override as_sql() for vendor features |\n\n### Data Flow Description\n\n1. **Filter Definition Phase**\n   ```\n   Model.objects.filter(name='John', age__gt=18)\n   \u2193\n   QuerySet._filter_or_exclude_inplace() parses kwargs\n   \u2193\n   Query.add_filter() creates Lookup('name', 'John'), Lookup('age__gt', 18)\n   \u2193\n   WhereNode.children = [Lookup(...), Lookup(...)]\n   \u2193\n   Query.setup_joins() adds necessary JOINs to alias_map\n   ```\n\n2. **Compilation Phase**\n   ```\n   SQLCompiler.as_sql()\n   \u2193\n   for each expression in self.select:\n       compile(expression) \u2192 expression.as_sql(compiler, connection)\n   \u2193\n   compile(where_node)\n       \u2193 WhereNode.as_sql()\n       \u251c\u2500 for each child (Lookup):\n       \u2502   \u251c\u2500 compile(child)\n       \u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500 Lookup.as_sql()\n       \u2502   \u2502       \u251c\u2500 process_lhs() \u2192 compile(lhs_expression)\n       \u2502   \u2502       \u2514\u2500 process_rhs() \u2192 compile(rhs_value)\n       \u2502   \u2514\u2500 accumulate SQL and params\n       \u2514\u2500 \" AND \".join() or \" OR \".join()\n   \u2193\n   Result: (\"SELECT id, name FROM app_model WHERE name = %s AND age > %s\", ['John', 18])\n   ```\n\n3. **Execution Phase**\n   ```\n   cursor.execute(sql, params)\n   \u2193\n   Database returns raw rows\n   \u2193\n   for each row:\n       Model.from_db(db, fields, row_data) \u2192 Model instance\n   \u2193\n   QuerySet iteration yields Model instances\n   ```\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n1. **Expression Protocol**\n   - `as_sql(compiler, connection)` \u2192 `(sql_string, params_list)`\n   - `resolve_expression(query, ...)` \u2192 resolved Expression instance\n   - `get_source_expressions()` \u2192 `[expr, ...]`\n\n2. **Compiler Protocol**\n   - `compile(node)` \u2192 `(sql_string, params_list)` (dispatcher to as_sql/as_vendor)\n   - `setup_query()` \u2192 side effect: sets self.select, self.klass_info, self.annotation_col_map\n   - `execute_sql(result_type)` \u2192 results (rows, row count, cursor, or empty)\n\n3. **Lookup Protocol** (extends Expression)\n   - `process_lhs(compiler, connection)` \u2192 `(sql_string, params_list)`\n   - `process_rhs(compiler, connection)` \u2192 `(sql_string, params_list)`\n   - `get_rhs_op(connection, rhs_sql)` \u2192 formatted operator + RHS (e.g., `\"= %s\"`)\n\n4. **Backend Operations Protocol**\n   - `compiler(compiler_name)` \u2192 SQLCompiler class\n   - `quote_name(identifier)` \u2192 quoted identifier\n   - Database feature flags (supports_select_for_update, has_bulk_insert, etc.)\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nDjango's ORM query compilation follows a **lazy evaluation + multi-phase compilation** architecture. High-level QuerySet operations build an abstract SQL representation (Query object with annotations, JOINs, and WhereNode predicates) without executing. When evaluation is triggered, the **SQLCompiler walks the Query AST and recursively compiles each Expression/Lookup via the as_sql() protocol**, using a **vendor dispatch pattern** (as_{vendor}() methods) to support database-specific dialects. The **WhereNode tree** elegantly handles nested logical filters, while the **Lookup system** abstracts filter syntax (\"field__lookup=value\") into bidirectional SQL compilation. This design separates query building from SQL generation, enabling complex query composition while remaining flexible for database vendor customization.\n",

# Django ORM Query Compilation Pipeline Analysis

## Files Examined

### Core QuerySet & Manager (Entry Points)
- **django/db/models/manager.py** — Manager class providing `get_queryset()` entry point that creates QuerySet instances; serves as the public API surface for model queries
- **django/db/models/query.py** — QuerySet class implementing lazy query construction; holds reference to Query object and manages result caching, filtering, ordering, and iteration; delegates SQL generation to Query compiler

### SQL Query Representation Layer
- **django/db/models/sql/query.py** — Query class representing abstract SQL statement structure; stores table aliases, WHERE conditions, JOIN information, annotations, GROUP BY, ORDER BY; implements `get_compiler()` method for obtaining backend-specific compiler
- **django/db/models/sql/where.py** — WhereNode class representing tree-structured WHERE clause predicates using AND/OR/XOR connectors; recursively compiles child expressions to SQL

### SQL Compilation Layer
- **django/db/models/sql/compiler.py** — SQLCompiler class (and subclasses SQLInsertCompiler, SQLUpdateCompiler, SQLDeleteCompiler) that generates SQL from Query; implements `as_sql()` method assembling SELECT, FROM, WHERE, GROUP BY, HAVING, ORDER BY, LIMIT/OFFSET clauses; implements `execute_sql()` for executing compiled SQL against database
- **django/db/models/sql/datastructures.py** — BaseTable, Join, MultiJoin classes representing table aliases and JOIN structures in query

### Expression System (Composable SQL Building Blocks)
- **django/db/models/expressions.py** — BaseExpression class defining Expression protocol with `as_sql()` method for SQL code generation; subclasses include Value (literals), F (field references), Col (column references), Case/When (condition
... (truncated)
